## \#47 Posted by: RunPlayBack Posted at: 2016-02-08T14:47:47.170Z Reads: 701

```
I plan to tackle some trails when the weather warms up. Do you roughly estimate your speed and distance to measure when you need to head back to your car or just wing it?
```

---
## \#48 Posted by: longhairedboy Posted at: 2016-02-08T15:32:04.376Z Reads: 741

```
Being uber familiar with the trails helps, but yes, that's exactly what i do: roughly estimate and wing it. I turn around at 52% battery if my guess of the halfway point hasn't arrived yet and attempt to maintain the same kind of riding style on the way back. So far that way of doing it has not failed me. 

The trail in that video is 4.87 miles long from my parking spot to the board-walk dead end where i turn around, which makes for a ~9.7 mile ride total. My 220Wh 6S (The Red Baroness, which is currently dead, needs battery) can make that ride provided i keep it below 15mph (which for me is run out speed, barely need pads or helmet or anything, so sometimes i don't wear any gear and just sip my soda the whole way and let me hair fly). Scarlet is running a re-packed space cell, so its a 10S 270Wh board and can make that trip while averaging almost 20mph, which means plenty of top-out stretches as long as i keep the cruise more casual at some points. It also means i'm wearing a helmet and I have pads under my hoodie and jeans. 

My next build is going to be a 12S 12Ah ~530Wh single drive 6372ish graphene lipo build and I'm going to utterly murder that trail from start to finish, possibly twice in a row. Sometime this year, i may have the extra cash for my personal ride to update it and do this. My propdrive 270s are still killing it, but i think The Baroness will likely end up on a shelf as a conversation peice if i can't find "the right" pack for it.
```

---
## \#49 Posted by: mostwanted Posted at: 2016-02-09T02:27:27.257Z Reads: 762

```
i posted this video on my facebook page and a fellow skater comments ~ "sounds like a mad scientist"  . well then , i am !. i'm not hurt by that comment . i see it as a complement . just a crazy mad most wanted scientist that never get to invent anything .

i 1st found out about electric skateboard was in sept 2014 . spent 8 hours watching youtube videos just about electric skate/longboard .
got my 24v 1st brush dc motor ready made eboard the next few days .

got my 1st brushless dc motor , dual diagonal kit at 30th sept 2015 . got it all fixed & wired up on 16th oct 2015 . dc wiring are easy to understand . when it comes to bldc , i'm new to it . thanks to a fellow eboarder  whom once in a while advices & educate me on certain times he is available .

so , in all i took SIXTEEN days to figure out which wire goes to which connectors and finally , i just gotta record my 1st spinning wheels . watch . the one with red wheels are the weak and slow HUMONGOUS dc motor eboard .



https://youtu.be/sqw1KG7ifSg
```

## \#54 Posted by: Howser Posted at: 2016-02-17T17:30:14.782Z Reads: 655

```
yes! they where 30-40km/h fast and extremely loud (chainsaw motor). because of the noise, all motorized skateboards / bikes / scooters where banned in California. New eboards etc. automatically fell under this law up until it was finally lifted recently to accommodate to the new technology
```

```
in singapore , you can get a $500 ticket if plain~clothes National Environment Agency officer catches you . they will wait for you to completely slow down and have a rest (sitting probably) and demand for identity card . and issue a $500 ticket .  you can of course appeal (if granted) for reduced $100 ticket . so far i never encounter any of them , police or other government agencies .
```

## \#68 Posted by: mostwanted Posted at: 2016-02-19T15:28:59.144Z Reads: 636

```
we have .

https://www.facebook.com/groups/1198184386874565/


just that most of us are too busy flying to  L.A .   California ,  Australia  , Japan ,  probably 3 are foreigners  working in Singapore , and local students busy with exams e.t.c .

from that point Marina Bay Sands , one can skate til the end of the island in the east , where our International Airport is located about 25km estimated distance .

in the video it looks fast , but actually its not . i was just testing on my 1st day of eboard completion . 

theres many plain clothes officer with speed check meter gun and a high definition 1080p camera  hiding . ever so ready to catch speed demon . even normal cyclist and in line skaters got a $500 ticket for exceeding the 25km/h limit . 
they always work in team of 4 to 7 officers . 1 officer at 1st point with speed gun , 2nd and third will be 100m away with camera . the rest will just need confirmation from the first 3  officer , and they stopped offender and issue ticket . easy MONEY !

same advice and scenario depicted in this video from Enertions

https://youtu.be/o_5Bh4zceGQ

some area says 25km/h , while some only 15km/h . so be carefull when in singapore parks .   just dont speed .
```

## \#69 Posted by: longhairedboy Posted at: 2016-02-19T15:59:06.909Z Reads: 619

```
where i live we have so much actual crime that nobody is watching the bike trails. they're 15mph too but every single spandex coated cyclist out there is doing at least 30mph and they're doing it in packs of 5 or more. We have some serious cyclists in my area. You actually NEED an electric skateboard to keep up with them. 

I often mention passing and buzzing the cyclists but truth be told, a lot of them can't be buzzed or passed without achieving speeds requiring full armor. They're too busy pumping for 100 miles straight while maintaining relatively high speeds on their $10,000 bikes to be bothered. I do try to keep up with them though, its fun and often starts good conversations while i'm just standing there sipping a coke at 25mph. 

I also don't ride in downtown areas, parks, or other places where people are just derping around. To me that's just asking for trouble. In the past i've done so and have been harassed by pedestrians.
```

## \#76 Posted by: Namasaki Posted at: 2016-03-05T02:36:54.360Z Reads: 573

```
Why go 80% when you can go 100%?
Why have limits?
With TB's 12s Esc's and mini RC Remote, control is very good at 100%. I can easily cruise at 5-10 mph
or 10-20mph. And quickly wind it up to 25-30 mph
30 is the fastest I've gone so far. I still haven't maxed it out.
Everyone is saying that Vesc is tops. 
But I liked the robust design of the TB's with there huge heat sinks. And quick easy programming. 
I have worked them very hard and they just keep on going with no problems or issues. They are very responsive with no lag at all.
```

## \#103 Posted by: JT_Clemente Posted at: 2016-03-07T05:44:40.321Z Reads: 482

```
Just a heads up, GoPros do not have standard tripod holes. You will need a GoPro tripod adapter in order to mount it to that pole!
Edit: I didn't see the top picture, you will be able to mount your GoPro to the top picture, but not the second one with the 1/4 tripod screw!
```

```
1080/60
1080/30
720/60

720/60 was much smoother
Looks like 720/60 is better option for fast motion video.
```

## \#164 Posted by: Namasaki Posted at: 2016-03-14T13:41:37.426Z Reads: 344

```
So, I tried to edit with iMovie but found out that it only supports 30fps. 
I shot the video at 720/60. So I went out and got
Adobe Premiere Elements14 and used it for edit. 
It supports up to 1080/60 and was much easier to edit with than iMovie.
It also rendered the movie fairly quickly into an MP4 file that is only about 188mb so it uploaded to YouTube very quickly. I played it back full screen on my 42" Flat screen and it looked pretty good and smooth.
```

## \#173 Posted by: Namasaki Posted at: 2016-03-14T18:47:47.372Z Reads: 364

```
The gimbal is small and light. along with the Gopro sessions, its not bad. I had it on a fairly light pole and it was fine.
One really good thing about the gimbal is that it always keeps the camera level no mater what you do. So you can move the pole around all over the place without even thinking about it. It was well worth every penny!
I have since upgraded to a Gopole which is much sturdier. I sent the R1 back to amazon because it did not have full functionality with the sessions model as it does with older Gopro's like hero3. And the battery would drain too fast.
I got the Gopro smart remote which is smaller, water proof,doesn't drain its battery fast at all and lets me change camera settings right from remote. The R1 would not do camera settings with the sessions model. The free iPhone app works better than the R1. With live view on a bigger and better screen and full control of settings and media. Oh, and you can have both the phone app and the smart remote connected and controling the camera at the same time! And if you change camera settings with the remote, it updates the screen on the phone app and visa versa
```

---
## \#174 Posted by: Michaelinvegas Posted at: 2016-03-14T19:23:33.163Z Reads: 373

```
Yeah the R1 is mostly just to line up shots when you don't want to use your phone in high risk situations....wifi just sucks battery no matter what...<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/8/8084df37ea98f5d4343a92e695584658de8ce67b.jpg" width="375" height="500"> 
I have on of these that I attach to a lipo battery...I can recharge things all day long...especially if your out and abt and filming all day and don't have enough spare batteries .... And you can charge everyone's phone lol
```

## \#202 Posted by: RunPlayBack Posted at: 2016-04-02T21:08:58.318Z Reads: 332

```
Yeah I'm still trying to figure out different techniques of riding but with high speed carving I seem to get into a crouching position by instinct. The protective gear that I wear is a Bern Brenwood Helmet, Sector 9 elbow and knee pads, Sector 9 Boxer II sliding gloves, leather joggers and sometimes a neoprene/fleece scarf.
```

## \#216 Posted by: makevoid Posted at: 2016-04-09T09:07:40.397Z Reads: 344

```
Hi all, I just finished this build with Enertion single motor kit, a 6S battery and a 100A ESC, that's like my 5th ride on it. Finally I have a board that is reliable, my first build was with chinese hub motors and they overheated and failed (I burned 1 motor and 2 ESCs), then I watched @onloop's video on motors and decided to go with the Enertion kit, this motor is so big it can't basically hoverheat, all my rides were very smooth even if my build is a bit rough :) I will make a post on the other section soon.


This is the video:

https://youtu.be/5pwhRvsEbt4


I used a smartphone to record + a Zhiyun Z1 stabilizer, that was my first time testing it and overall I'm satisfied of the results, tell me what you think!
```

```
I was still sleepy (6am) and afraid of falling with the new gimbal or breaking it because of the rain lol.
```

## \#223 Posted by: RunPlayBack Posted at: 2016-04-09T23:24:07.845Z Reads: 304

```
@makevoid @Michaelinvegas I pretty much approach DIY camera stuff the same way I approach ESK8.  So many different ways to get to the final product that it doesn't really matter what you use, as long as you learn something and it fits within your means. There's no right or wrong way as long as you keep shooting and discovering new techniques. And while I've had my share of big budget music videos and commercials, none of those gigs really compare to capturing a genuine moment with whatever you can get your hands on. Success in videos has never really been about budgets for me anyway, it's always been about how valuable I could make myself to others.
```

---

It was good meeting you too, @Michaelinvegas , next time I'll try not to rip two belts until after we get some video.

## \#239 Posted by: onloop Posted at: 2016-04-20T14:13:40.423Z Reads: 282


---
## \#240 Posted by: RunPlayBack Posted at: 2016-04-20T14:21:35.684Z Reads: 294

```
They know me by face because I attend NAB each year but their marketing team caught hold of my DIY eboard camera rig video so they knew I was using their gimbal to shoot. So NAB stands for the National Association of Broadcasters and it's the biggest video technology show of the year. International attendees represent every sector of the industry including broadcast tv, digital media, film, entertainment, post production, VR, etc. It's massive and super fun if you are into video. I've been posting a bunch of the latest tech [on my Instagram account](http://instagram.com/rikcordero) if anyone wants to see what they have out here.

https://www.instagram.com/p/BEXIf9PtHgE/?taken-by=rikcordero
```

## \#265 Posted by: makevoid Posted at: 2016-04-25T23:36:23.933Z Reads: 261

```
Nice video, you go very fast on that road! 

I think that youtube converted it to 30fps, it doesn't show me the 720p60 option as other 60fps videos do I don't know why :/ . 
I think the best advantage of recording at 60fps is that you can slow down the clip at 50% and still have enough frame rate to be viewable without using smooth filters like final cut optical flow or similar. Don't get me wrong, they are useful to bring the speed even to a lower point but a higher frame rate is a good place to start :slight_smile:.
```

## \#374 Posted by: thisrealhuman Posted at: 2016-06-15T03:30:23.225Z Reads: 279

```
[quote="RunPlayBack, post:372, topic:47, full:true"]
I love your Google Earth Pro videos! How do you make the path draw with the arrow icon?
[/quote]


Step one, Get [Maverick for Android](https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.codesector.maverick.lite&hl=en&gl=us), it records all your GPS data into a .GPX file.
Step two, Get [Google Earth Pro](https://www.google.com/earth/), It's FREE now in case you didn't know.
Step three, open the GPX file with Earth and it creates the path and arrow. There's an elevation profile too, but I haven't put any effort into getting that into the video yet. 

Once you have the path loaded, select it under the TRACKS folder and click the "Play Tour" button under my small red arrow. This brings up the slider with a save button under my big red arrow. it will save your tour at the bottom of the Places list, click on the tour and Save to My Places.
<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/6/6a2c2c31e484749f5b7feac8a630eff68d9bf049.jpg" width="400" height="500">
Next click tools, Movie Maker. You get the option to record a saved tour, but ONLY if it's Saved in My Places.
<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/8/8ffbb0ccbb246cfa6cc1dad6089bcea341e7b66e.jpg" width="690" height="367">
The path and arrow only show up if you have them checked in the temporary places. Video quality settings are up to you and your system's abilities.
```

---

## \#398 Posted by: chaka Posted at: 2016-06-19T18:28:31.511Z Reads: 285

```
@RunPlayBack I noticed you like to stinkbug on your board a lot. It is going to be a hard habit to break and can get you in trouble as you progress. Leads to poor weight distribution and can give you some mean wobbles if you are not careful.
```

---
## \#399 Posted by: RunPlayBack Posted at: 2016-06-19T18:53:00.976Z Reads: 290

```
@chaka Yeah, I sprained my push foot last week so I couldn't really put much weight on my back leg heel, even flexing it right now is a little painful. I probably shouldn't have been on a board but with that many people showing up I couldn't resist. My single hub with the 90mm ABEC's don't really slide and yesterday I had pretty stiff bushings on to avoid wobbling all together - mostly because of my foot/ankle and for anyone else who wanted to try the board. I'll probably need more practice on a non electric longboard with softer wheels to figure out my stance. Still learning.
```

---
## \#400 Posted by: chaka Posted at: 2016-06-19T21:21:22.753Z Reads: 291

```
I was referring to grabbing the board between your legs.  Here's a video of Cliff Coleman at a slide clinic explaining some tips on technique but if you google stinkbug grab you will get more info on the topic.  We are all guilty of it at some point ;)
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qcQpcvkylGs
```

---
## \#401 Posted by: RunPlayBack Posted at: 2016-06-19T21:45:54.193Z Reads: 286

```
So if I ride goofy and favor my ride hand for the controller, I have to switch to my left hand even though my wheels can't slide? I can try practicing that. But outside of stinkbug not being stylish for traditional downhill longboarding, I'm wondering how do the same techniques apply to the vast array of eboard builds that have a much different weight/rider distribution?
```

---
## \#402 Posted by: chaka Posted at: 2016-06-19T22:36:35.687Z Reads: 286

```
It has nothing to do with being stylish. Generally you will want to grab some rail going through a hard turn and if you are grabbing between you knees you will be at a severe disadvantage. Better to learn good form early on rather than build on bad habits. I don't mean any offense, just trying to point you in the right direction.
```

---

```

Especially as we have more riders come out to skate on video I want to share as much as possible to keep everyone safe. I always appreciate your feedback :)
```

## \#410 Posted by: RunPlayBack Posted at: 2016-06-23T13:06:35.559Z Reads: 273

```
@cmatson looks like you're having a great time, glad you got your controller working. Would you say the skate shops out there are more receptive to eboarding than in the states? Have you come across any other eboarders?
```

---
## \#411 Posted by: cmatson Posted at: 2016-06-23T21:47:59.493Z Reads: 276

```
I've seen about 8 or 9 guys riding eboards- that's more than I've seen in Jax back home. That said, I've been going all through melbourne and sydney, and some of the coastal areas in Sydney are absolutely perfect for an eboard-

Here, there are just enough hills to make a normal board a pain in the ass (downhill would be fast, uphill too steep) so electric boards make a ton of sense. Nothing a classic belt drive setup couldn't handle either. 

I think with this skate shop in particular though everyone who worked there and was in the shop at the time loved the idea and didn't think that it "threatened" classic skateboarding in any way- intact they didn't even mention it. 

So I guess it really depends on where you are.. Maybe a nice beach town in the US could have a bigger eboard population, but that's just my hunch.
```

```
This same thing happened to be last month except on my normal longboard. I was skating through a big parking lot leaving a movie theater when I to pick up a call from a friend. As I did this I hit a curb with one of my wheels and flew off my board. A passing car caught my board under its tire but the driver stopped before my board snapped. One of my wheels now has about a 1/4 of an inch angled flat spot on it cause it scraped against the pavement. At least my board is fine.
```

## \#527 Posted by: RunPlayBack Posted at: 2016-08-13T02:27:56.781Z Reads: 262

```
https://vimeo.com/178689405

Here's a pretty chill session we had last night at a local high school. Some good friends of mine and their kids have never tried ESK8 before so brought a few boards out for them to test and get comfortable. There's only a quick clip of me on the Carvon V2.5 hub but I mostly had the kids riding the Carvon EMC2 and my vintage mini cruiser with the speed limited. Sessions like these are super fun because it's just about building confidence and highlighting safety in a controlled area.
```

## \#529 Posted by: Kaly Posted at: 2016-08-13T14:38:08.370Z Reads: 256

```
Since I saw tha emc2 mini board. It is exactly what I envision a board that a kid can use and teach them the basics and get them to respect the esk8. 

Man you are always a step ahead. You are bless with the ability and have the dedication to put into images the emotional part of eSk8. :thumbsup: keep up the good work.
```

---
## \#530 Posted by: RunPlayBack Posted at: 2016-08-13T15:21:11.147Z Reads: 253

```
Yeah the EMC2 is nice board to get people comfortable with ESK8, especially kids. My Yuneec EGO used to be the beginner board but it's a little too big and bulky to transport. The EMC2 has a smooth, conservative curve on throttle and brake so as long as they can balance, it's easy for beginners to hop right on. I'd say this was one of the first times where we really focused on the communal family bonding aspect of ESK8 which is exactly what happened. The two kids didn't want to stop skating and the parents were really excited to discover this activity they can all participate in.
```

```
We had a fun ride today with the vintage mini cruisers in a newly asphalt paved, unused parking lot at a local college campus. Cops rolled by and didn't stop us. Today was a good day :) Also had a blast testing the Carvon V2.5 single hub motor which had incredible snappy torque and braking. It was even able to pull @Jeff who weighs 250+ lbs. Meetups like this make me super nostalgic.
```

## \#571 Posted by: jesser722 Posted at: 2016-08-31T17:26:13.658Z Reads: 268

```
Hey Guys! First Post here, I have spent this last summer building my first Electric longboard and it was the best decision I have ever made. I used a 230kv motor with 2 5000mah lips batteries in series. I cut the motor mount out of aluminum and welded it on my trucks. I used thin abs plastic for the cover and melted it to the correct shape. Let me know if you have an other questions and here is a video I made about the board: [My Summer Electric Longboard Project Video](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IqHIzKqaU7I)
```

## \#574 Posted by: Mrmoonlight Posted at: 2016-09-02T07:50:55.379Z Reads: 272

```
I rode about 4 miles over the Pulaski and up over to Kent, then up that stretch on 5th. So the board already had quite a workout before the bridge. If the board was cold, no problem, but I push past the first expansion joint then throttle it up as fast as I can, but still can't make it up to the merger. Have to push a little to get past the crest. 

Just got my v2.5 in. Haven't even opened the box yet. It'll solve any issues getting up the bridge. I'll take another vid for that.
```

## \#648 Posted by: sismeiro Posted at: 2016-10-10T19:16:51.216Z Reads: 236

```
@Spek It's not easy to make interesting videos for other people to see. Long videos can be boring if there isn't anything interesting to see or some music. I think you did well with yours. :slight_smile:

Check the videos in my channel and tell me what you think: [https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCgtpRNiXTr4WqpU5ZFnTpvQ/videos](https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCgtpRNiXTr4WqpU5ZFnTpvQ/videos)
```

---
## \#649 Posted by: Spek Posted at: 2016-10-10T19:38:55.673Z Reads: 237

```
Thanks for the feedback! Ill check out your channel for sure. 

Its definitely too long. I didn't have any time to edit and was just excited to share. In terms of the camera work, I was pretty happy with the results. I expected it to be much shakier without a gimble or anything and sometimes the selfie stick videos can be boring or disorienting. I was really trying to capture the sense of speed which I think I did.  I'll probably end up posting some edited stuff in the weeks to come as I gather more footage. 

Also the youtube stabilization went into effect overnight and really made it worse and I've since reverted it back to the original. It was zooming in and out to stabilize it and really made it look weird.
```

---
## \#650 Posted by: IDVert3X Posted at: 2016-10-10T19:43:58.674Z Reads: 244

```
YouTube ( and any other software ) is terrible in stabilazing your videos. There is just not enough data.

I was looking around for actions cameras with image stabilization and the Xiaomi Yi 2 looks really interesting.
Great image quality and video is pretty stable. For ~ 230 eur from China not that bad.

EDIT: review
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=28k7uBDojb8
```

---
## \#651 Posted by: Spek Posted at: 2016-10-10T19:47:31.505Z Reads: 240

```
I didn't even feel like my footage needed the stabilization, but youtube offer so I figured why not? Now I know. A little camera shake actually made the shots feel faster, to me.
```

```
Ya, they're too small. They come in different lengths.
I use these, they work better than anything the skate shops have.

```

---
## \#825 Posted by: wmj259 Posted at: 2017-02-26T02:28:07.923Z Reads: 185

```
Will try those out, so if these are larger, my bearings should stick out a little but correct? But if I take the wheel off the spacer shouldn't be sliding around, should be a right fit.
```

---
## \#826 Posted by: mmaner Posted at: 2017-02-26T02:31:23.235Z Reads: 188

```
Spacers a little complicated. It should be a snug (not tight) fit between the bearings. 

In my experience the spacers that come with buddy flywheels are too small.  I usually get them 2mm too large and then file them down a little bit at a time.  

Most people don't like the plastic spacers but I've found that they tend to perform better, but not for very long.  I bout 20 sets of plastic spacers and speed rings off eBay for around 2 bucks, don't remember exactly as it's been a few months.
```

---
## \#827 Posted by: Namasaki Posted at: 2017-02-26T02:45:53.356Z Reads: 183

```
I lock my wheels down tight with these spacers. 
Because they have thicker walls than most skate spacers they provide a very solid setup and my wheels spin for a long time. The fit really depends on the particular wheels your using. If they wind up being a little big, then I just let the wheels float on them a little because it would be very difficult if not impossible to file or hand grind them down while keeping the mating surface flat and square. You would really need a lathe to trim them  accurately.
```

---
## \#828 Posted by: mmaner Posted at: 2017-02-26T02:49:19.834Z Reads: 194

```
I'm gonna order some of those spacers, prolly sweet.  

BTW, the way you file them.is with a jig.  I don't have a pic, but it's essentially a piece of 2x4 drilled to hold the spacer tight horizontally and th exact depth you want vertically.  Set the 2x4 between to pieces of angle iron (which are clamped to a table top) with the file clamped underneath.  Then you just run it back and forth until it stops sanding.  I do 4 at a time usually.
```

---
## \#829 Posted by: Namasaki Posted at: 2017-02-26T06:29:39.910Z Reads: 199

```
I didn't think of making a jig. That's a great idea @mmaner
```

```
I've tried wearing motorcycle leathers while riding and though it made me feel more safe and even invincible. It made me feel  top heavy and really messed with my balance. The added weight was more than my legs are used to carrying so it prevented me from being relaxed and loose.
```

## \#934 Posted by: nmagz3 Posted at: 2017-04-11T22:38:24.625Z Reads: 195


---
## \#935 Posted by: RunPlayBack Posted at: 2017-04-11T23:57:19.137Z Reads: 195

```
Hey bro, it was through a friend of a friend - out here in MI, it's really about who you know and who vouches for you. We did a very quick test ride but created enough of a spectacle that every racer in the house was into it. We're still in the process of discussing insurance and liability but for something like this - only those 18 years old and up can be on the track.
```

## \#1143 Posted by: chaka Posted at: 2017-07-13T17:11:19.650Z Reads: 230

```
@JohnnyMeduse looks like you are using the 005ohm.bin firmware judging by the error in recording the watt usage. At 100amps the vesc dissipates 300 watts. This means you were only passing 50 amps in that video. #smoke&mirrors :joy:
```

---
## \#1145 Posted by: chaka Posted at: 2017-07-13T17:16:28.771Z Reads: 226

```
Show us a video of a stable temp and current and you might redeem yourself. But if you are using the 005om.bin the video will still show double the current that is actually being used.

I could be wrong? I see lower losses on our prototype version with 12 Toshiba MOSFETS but our temps do not climb as quickly as what you showed in your video.
```

## \#1148 Posted by: Mobutusan Posted at: 2017-07-15T23:28:27.174Z Reads: 222

```
@electricjim79 What kind of throttle lever setup are you using? I'm trying to figure out how to do a wired throttle with these TB 12s car esc's, so I can do a thumb throttle on my drift trike, and a proportional foot pedal throttle on my son's power wheels. Thanks!
```

---
## \#1149 Posted by: electricjim79 Posted at: 2017-07-16T10:17:13.617Z Reads: 224

```
Nothing overly technical, the whole thing is made up from reclaimed bits of electric scooters so the throttle is just the twist grip throttle of the handle bars bolted to the deck with a lever fixed to it
```

## \#1192 Posted by: ejbares Posted at: 2017-08-09T02:13:45.115Z Reads: 216

```
PLEASE do not give me hate! In fact help me by liking this video!

I'm mainly try to reach the kids that aren't already into this and trying to save them from wasting a lot of money or getting themselves hurt!

Please leave a comment to add to it if I missed something or if you have other input! (I'm just scared that I'm going to get a lot of hate from this when I'm just trying to help people)
```

## \#1193 Posted by: Battosaii Posted at: 2017-08-09T03:56:01.458Z Reads: 211

```
No hate its true some people buy expensive things because they think its cool then never use it but thats true with anything. I personally love cruising on my regular long board its so smooth and carvy but my electric board gives me those down hill speeds in a state with no hills, i use any excuse to use my board, not because i spent $1000 on it but because i find it incredibly fun and liberating.
```

---
## \#1194 Posted by: Namasaki Posted at: 2017-08-09T04:22:41.190Z Reads: 212

```
I started with a manual longboard and got tired of walking up hills.
Also I'm a surfer, so when I ride a skateboard, I like to carve back and forth like when I'm surfing.
Every time I would try to carve on my manual board, it would slow down even when going down mild hills.
So now I ride an electric longboard.
Now I can fly up hills and control my speed down hills without sliding and wearing my wheels out.
Now I can carve back and forth non stop without loosing momentum.
I would not want to go back to a manual board now.
So wether or not Electric is worth it is very subjective.
For you, it's not worth it.
For me it's well worth it.
```

---


## \#1229 Posted by: Namasaki Posted at: 2017-09-05T13:31:37.926Z Reads: 219

```
Im also using the Metr module and app and I like it but I have compared it with my onboard volt meter and my Fluke multimeter and found that it always displays the voltage about 0.6 volt higher than it really is. 
It's just something that you should be aware of and you might want to compare with a meter on your system.
```

---
## \#1230 Posted by: i2oadsweepei2 Posted at: 2017-09-05T13:42:02.178Z Reads: 214

```
Thank you. I will look into that.
```

```
It's the same for @Ackmaniac android telemetry app, it reads about .5v lower than actual pack voltage.
```

## \#1244 Posted by: rpasichnyk Posted at: 2017-09-08T17:43:19.861Z Reads: 209

```
This is just how VESC measures the voltage, not very accurate. If you open VESC Tool (BLDC Tool), you will see the same value as in metr app, .6 high. If you really want to fix this on your VESC, you can check this topic http://vedder.se/forums/viewtopic.php?t=217 measure resistance of your SMD resistor and compile special firmware with your unique value ;)
```

## \#1632 Posted by: Deckoz Posted at: 2018-04-05T21:37:37.769Z Reads: 217

```
Slav squat... Or ass to grass Olympic without Olympic shoe handicap. But thanks! Not alot of people can go that low  with their hips wide open and no buttwink ;)

Just a side note: I started flying this way because 
- sitting made me feel like I was sinking
- standing..haha yeah no equilibrium
- squating like this is how baby's learn to stand, it's a very self centering position. So I was in the middle of my first pack flying and went from sitting and sinking to standing and almost falling over, to this squat where I immediately felt control and it stuck
```

## \#1676 Posted by: sayekim Posted at: 2018-04-28T08:21:05.044Z Reads: 210

```
Is that rubber instead of pu?

So the thin pu arguments on hub motors doesn‚Äôt apply here then for the feel of the wheels?
```

---
## \#1677 Posted by: MoeStooge Posted at: 2018-04-28T13:04:25.645Z Reads: 216

```
You know it's no good for race rubber to sit on the shelf..    @sayekim. The wheels are built completely different than the PU thin thane argument.   1/4" hard density foam with rubber overlay..  Designed for  high speed high grip application..  the ride quality just happens to be fantastic.  We're working on version for the World Record board with a lower roll resistance. My hope is that they retain the ride quality but offer a better cruising option with the lower roll resistance of urethane and the grip levels of pnumatics.. time and testing will tell.
```

## \#1953 Posted by: ksfacinelli Posted at: 2018-09-18T15:18:11.502Z Reads: 182

```
Here is a quick spin up video of @Hummie hubs on bench. The setup is using 10s4p @psychotiller battery and setup Focboxs with FOC. Have not got them on road yet due to rain however even the short time during setup seemed to loosen the grease in the bearings. I am also running at a switching frequency of 30 kHz and 100 amp max motor current and 60 amp max battery.  I think they are pretty quite no high pitch noise but you be the judge.  Would love to here from others regarding setups.

https://youtu.be/_2Qt-We4hqg
```

## \#2125 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2018-12-03T17:23:17.834Z Reads: 180

```
Can u get a drone to ride beside you at like 2ft high?  That would give a greater impression of the speed, and could get a mic done right for a bit of motor sound on the music.
```

---
## \#2126 Posted by: mmaner Posted at: 2018-12-03T17:26:57.703Z Reads: 183

```
The drone won't stay that close, it actually uses GPS positioning to the controller.  About 20 ft is as good as it gets.  I have a pretty pricey Tascam aural mic audio recorder, if you want really accurate audio.  A selfie stick or another rider is the only way I know to get that kind of video.  That being said, @sender and I have a plan to do just that using counterweighted handheld video recorder mounted to another board (mine) and a follow plan with your hummies.
```
